  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0e6491ac-d86d-4591-bf5b-e1d0006fd58d'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer7787291635166615656">For the millions who log in every day, Warcross isn’t just a game—it’s a way of life.   <span id="freeText7787291635166615656" style="display:none">For the millions who log in every day, Warcross isn’t just a game—it’s a way of life. The obsession started ten years ago and its fan base now spans the globe, some eager to escape from reality and others hoping to make a profit. Struggling to make ends meet, teenage hacker Emika Chen works as a bounty hunter, tracking down players who bet on the game illegally. But the bounty hunting world is a competitive one, and survival has not been easy. Needing to make some quick cash, Emika takes a risk and hacks into the opening game of the international Warcross Championships—only to accidentally glitch herself into the action and become an overnight sensation.<br /><br />Convinced she’s going to be arrested, Emika is shocked when instead she gets a call from the game’s creator, the elusive young billionaire Hideo Tanaka, with an irresistible offer. He needs a spy on the inside of this year’s tournament in order to uncover a security problem . . . and he wants Emika for the job. With no time to lose, Emika’s whisked off to Tokyo and thrust into a world of fame and fortune that she’s only dreamed of. But soon her investigation uncovers a sinister plot, with major consequences for the entire Warcross empire.</span>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Marie Lu has said that Warcross is set about ten years in our future, whereas Legend is set a hundred years from now. So Warcross takes place before L<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Marie Lu has said that Warcross is set about ten years in our future, whereas Legend is set a hundred years from now. So Warcross takes place before Legend, and Daniel Batu Wing, the stuntman who is mentioned in Warcross and Asher's older brother, is an ancestor, not descendant, of Day (Daniel Altan Wing).<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1175623'><a id="like_count_community_question_1175623" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1175623?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">10 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F41014903-warcross">like</a></span>

<a href="/questions/1175623-yeah-so-def-spoiler-question-am-i-one">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1175623-yeah-so-def-spoiler-question-am-i-one">See all 12 answers</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/61946844-amy"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1482455142i/61946844._UX100_CR0,11,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/61946844-amy">Amy</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The algorithm is something that sounds like a good idea at first, but has more and more problems the more you think about it. <br/><br/>What, exactly, does the <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The algorithm is something that sounds like a good idea at first, but has more and more problems the more you think about it. <br /><br />What, exactly, does the algorithm stop? Is it only overt physical violence? In that case, what about people who act maliciously toward others, but do so without physical violence, like the boy who took the nude photo of Annie without her knowledge or consent, then posted it publicly? What about people who act violently but not maliciously, like a person who is defending themselves? What about people that do not view their actions as being harmful to others, such as someone who is truly delusional or psychotic? There is a relatively common yardstick of criminal culpability known as the M'Naghten Rule; it basically states that people who are so deranged as to not know either (1) the nature or quality of their actions or (2) that what they are doing is wrong are not criminal but mentally ill. The algorithm doesn't care about criminal culpability except to prevent it, but therein lies the point: if a person's perception of the world is so distorted by psychosis that they don't realize, say, plowing their car into oncoming traffic will kill other drivers, how would the algorithm interpret, intervene, and prevent the action based on the psychotic individual's own perceptions? <br /><br />Self harm is clearly something to stopped at all costs under the algorithm, but I doubt the reason for self harm considered (after all, the algorithm is not conscious). What if the person is someone seeking assistance under the death with dignity/physician assisted suicide laws, and the algorithm has merely prolonged senseless suffering by preventing them from using medication procured for that purpose? Also, because the algorithm is not conscious, I somehow doubt that person is encouraged to seek mental health assistance in the aftermath of a failed attempt to self harm. In these cases, the algorithm preventing self harming behavior has done nothing to actually help the person in the long term unless it prevents what would have been a successful suicide for reasons other than death with dignity. <br /><br />Those are just the things that I could think of within a minute or two of reading Hideo's justification. I agree with some of the other posters here about liking that Hideo is a sympathetic villain. However, we shouldn't forget that he IS a villain. We shouldn't forget the human psychology and behavior are extremely complicated, and that there are always exceptions to every rule. We shouldn't forget that coding, algorithms, and computers work best in narrow circumstances that have a discrete set of potential outcomes and a single, clearly right answer. We shouldn't forget that human life is nothing like that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

</div>
<ul class='communityQAFooter answerFooter'>
</ul>

</div>
</div>

</div>

</div>

      <a class="uitext" id="span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_391" style="cursor: pointer; " href="#" onclick="return false"><span class="gr-hyperlink">Sort order</span></a><script>

<div id="review_1982074617" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982074617" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982074617?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep-side">lgbtq-rep-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=ya-sff">ya-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982074617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1498406874623063074">I want dwayne the rock to bench press me I'm pretty sure it'll hurt less than whatever is happening right now.<br/><br/>This was so fucking INCREDIBLE and like...ohm y god I'm just <b>[takes deep breath] <br/><br/>[dinosaur noises]</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“They believe that objects have souls. The more love you put into one, the more beautiful it becomes.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500617838i/23365674._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu' title='Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marie Lu</a> said this book was “<b>a love letter to all [her] favourite things</b>” and I keep imagining a tree that died and got chopped up into tiny pieces to become stardust that will find us a</span>
  <span id="freeText1498406874623063074" style="display:none">I want dwayne the rock to bench press me I'm pretty sure it'll hurt less than whatever is happening right now.<br><br>This was so fucking INCREDIBLE and like...ohm y god I'm just <b>[takes deep breath] <br><br>[dinosaur noises]</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“They believe that objects have souls. The more love you put into one, the more beautiful it becomes.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500617838i/23365674._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a> said this book was “<b>a love letter to all [her] favourite things</b>” and I keep imagining a tree that died and got chopped up into tiny pieces to become stardust that will find us again after billions of years and write us a perfumed love letter dusted in golden light and signed with a kiss…<b>in the form of this book.</b><br><br>ok I'm just being dramatic but seriously...reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> was like this weird holiday special from the universe that I've never expected and that was also the goddamn best feeling in the world I want to marry it!!<br><br>*sprays rose water on this book*<br><br><blockquote>so. <b><u>what is warcross about?</u></b>
</blockquote><br><br>You know when you read about a world and have those moments of warmth when you're daydreaming about a reality that you want and wish you could make for yourself?? that overwhelming urge to be a <i>part</i> of the story and not just read about it??<br><br>See, I’m here but I’m only here because I haven’t learned how to hack myself into warcross yet.<br><br>So, here's how the story goes:<br><br><b>Emika Chen</b>. A tattooed, rainbow haired, skateboarding bounty hunteress hacks into the opening ceremony of a world-wide well-known virtual game: Warcross.<br><br><b>What follows:</b> Tokyo. A 10 million offer. A last-minute player. Dark net. Illegal auctions. Unexpected friendships. And more than anything Emika has ever signed up for.<br><br>Trust me when I say that this book will take you to surprising emotional places. It's <b>action-packed</b>, <b>fast-paced </b>and the equivalent of having a million clementines thrown at your body at the same time. There will be moments when you'll be so incredibly emotional and high strung and anxious and overall bursting at the seams and moments that would feel like you'd been hit over the head with a baseball bat and then told to just forget about it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500613592i/23365160.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ <b>
  <u>WARCROSS THE GAME // VIRTUAL REALITY</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Some people still say that Warcross is just a stupid game. Others say it's a revolution. But for me and millions of others, it's the only foolproof way to forget our troubles. [...]tonight, I can join in with everyone else, put on my glasses, and watch magic happen.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Warcross</b> is actually more than a video game. See, it's like a real-time window into some alternate reality where you can transcend space and time and logic to hunt down artifacts and eliminate your foes. It's iconic and also the allegory for the emotional experience of existence<b> for every gamer</b> and it now offically joins <a href="http://fr.harrypotter.wikia.com/wiki/Quidditch" rel="nofollow noopener">quidditch</a> and <a href="http://foxhole-court.wikia.com/wiki/Exy" rel="nofollow noopener">exy</a> as the only three activities that have ever truly brought me joy in this unending hellscape of a life!!<br><br>I've never wanted more than to be awake and untrapped within the physics of this body and be physically transported into that realm, just to <b>play the fucking Warcross game</b>.... uuh never mind the fact that every competitive match I've ever played was just me as a support consistently thanking my teammates for saving my life or the fact that when I got my first gameboy and played Super Mario with such a deranged and obsessive tenacity that I would literally shut down the game whenever the ending wasn’t towards my favor .....LET ME LIVE!!<br><br>You know what though? here's an especially big <b>Fuck You</b> to technology for not stepping up her game and being beaten with a bound bundle of dead tree. Because this book made me really realize the things we could probably be doing with our time and advanced understanding of technology... anything <i>other</i> than 360 degree selfies and windows 10.<br><br>Just how is it 2017 and I can't walk out of my house with glitter lipstick and virtually shimmering skin, full body highlight and virtual knee length hair. I have virtual wings and a virtual tiger pet trotting at my side (this is actually canon in the book). For fuck's sake, I can’t even print out an essay without scraping out the eardrums of everyone in a 50m radius!!!!!<br><br>✨ <b>
  <u>CHARACTERS:</u>
</b><br><br>Do you ever meet a fictional character and suddenly you're hit with a wave of love so comfortable and deep that you feel like you've already loved this person for thousands of years??<br><br>This is literally about everyone is this book.<br><br><b>Warcross</b> was just good at handling the characters that I could actually hear their dialogue in their voices and actually imagine the scenarios being presented and wish I could astral project into their bodies and watch it all play out!!<br><br>We have such a <b>diverse</b> cast of characters with told stories that are so vague and so unique and so complexe and untold stories that will make you wish you could time travel to 2018 and read the sequel asap.<br><br>But mainly, <b>Emika Chen</b> with her rainbow hair, her sleeve tattoos and her attitude that resembles a rough sketch of something nice. <b>Hideo Tanaka </b> who's made of sugar spice and everything kind but also made of carbon atoms and lies (also, he has a british accent and wears nice shirts with his sleeves rolled up to the elbows and also cooks for his parents??? where's my inhaler I might breathe out my kidneys)<br><br>And <b>the rest of the characters</b> who captain teams and are super talented and can code and hack technology while I'm just here on the internet exploring the existential dread that’s latent in all of us and waiting for memes to come my way because I'm just a passive meme consumer not even contributing anything to the meme economy!!<br><br>✨ <b>
  <u> THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br><br>The fact that I am making an entire section just about this is prove enough of my passion. Aka, <b>I SHIP IT SO FUCKIGN HARD YOU GUYS</b>.<br><br>I’m trying to deconstruct my ideas about romantic love especially the ship where person A is a successful billionaire and person B is a penniless outlaw but it's really hard when my reptile brain literally has the phrase “<b>I SHIP IT</b>” on repeat!! like I know better but I also can’t help myself from giving into this brand of brainwashing. I guess my heart is just too soft when it comes to this trope…..I have a marshmallow heart.... a cotton candy heart.. a goddamn foam mattress heart!!<br><br>Anyways, thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a> for the new unexpected obsession, that was nice and cruel...<b>JUST LIKE THAT ENDING.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500515856i/23352705.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Reread 10/17:</b> if you're looking for me, I'll be in the trash BECAUSE THAT'S EXACTLY WHAT I AM FOR THIS BOOK!!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1498406874623063074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1566259389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566259389" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566259389?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=typical">typical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=lgbtqia-if-you-squint">lgbtqia-if-you-squint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=razor-sharp-wheels">razor-sharp-wheels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-am-so-smart-smrt">i-am-so-smart-smrt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=my-what-a-coincidence">my-what-a-coincidence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=when-sparks-don-t-fly">when-sparks-don-t-fly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=awesome-author">awesome-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=good-but-not-great">good-but-not-great</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566259389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3938892815561185428"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Cynical Natalie:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509201490ra/24299620.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Nice Natalie: For the record, I'm not comfortable being here. Marie Lu is one of our favorite authors! Remember when we <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449039674' rel='nofollow noopener'>met her</a> and acted like complete dorks, but she was still really nice?<br/><br/>Cynical Natalie: How many times do I have to tell you? Separate the person from the art. Marie Lu is a lovely person, but that doesn't mean I'm not going to rip into her brain baby's ass and yank its innards from its throat.<br/><br/>Nice Natalie: Must you be so vulgar?<br/><br/>Cynical Natalie: Yes. Besi</span>
  <span id="freeText3938892815561185428" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Cynical Natalie:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509201490ra/24299620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nice Natalie: For the record, I'm not comfortable being here. Marie Lu is one of our favorite authors! Remember when we <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449039674" rel="nofollow noopener">met her</a> and acted like complete dorks, but she was still really nice?<br><br>Cynical Natalie: How many times do I have to tell you? Separate the person from the art. Marie Lu is a lovely person, but that doesn't mean I'm not going to rip into her brain baby's ass and yank its innards from its throat.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Must you be so vulgar?<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Yes. Besides, you can't deny feeling thoroughly underwhelmed by Warcross.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Thoroughly is a bit of an overstatement. We did like the tournaments and the rules surrounding it. They were creative.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Wish she'd put some of that creativity towards the romance. It's bland as fuck and twice as squicky when you see it's eerily similar to Fifty Shades of Grey. Hot billionaire falls in love with a girl lower on the social/wealth rung for no apparent reason, pays all her bills, then flies her out to Tokyo on a private jet.<br><br>Nice Natalie: That's unfair! You can't lump all billionaire romances together with Fifty Shades.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: I can and I will. Books aren't written in a vacuum. She should have realized Hideo and Emika resembled Christian and Ana.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Emika isn't anything like Ana, nor Hideo like Christian. She's spirited and clever and stubborn—<br><br>Cynical Natalie: God, I hate the description "stubborn." Bella Swan and every TSTL Paranormal Romance heroine after her pulverized that word to watery soup. It's not even an insult anymore. It's a compliment dressed like a nightmare. <br><br>If you ask me, Emika is June 2.0. Her criminal record, the one that haunts her permanent record, making her *gasp* morally grey, is the result of her defending the weak. Her soul is vanilla through and through. Why couldn't she have gotten it by doing something selfish but also sympathetic, like hacking bank accounts to pay the bills after her dad died?<br><br>Nice Natalie: Just because you're going through an antihero phase doesn't make good characters bad.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Hey, I love Wonder Woman just as much as you, and she's as pure-hearted as they come. To prove, I'll tag a gif:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509201490ra/24299621.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I don't like are <i>boring</i> characters. One-note caricatures. <br><br>Plus, Emika's relationship with her dad is tragically one-dimensional. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23437156.Six_of_Crows__Six_of_Crows___1_" title="Six of Crows (Six of Crows, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a>, Kaz Brekker shares a nuanced, layered relationship with his decreased brother. Jordie had been wrongfully swindled, but part of the blame lay in his greed, and Kaz recognizes that. He's able to see his brother as a victim and the protector who abandoned him, no matter how unwillingly. <br><br>Emika and her father's relationship could've been something like that. Rage for him dying, for the debts, for leaving her alone and penniless. Love for the memories, for inspiring her rainbow-colored hair, for never forgetting to ask about her day. Instead we get a flat I-miss-him narrative. I could forgive it in her debut novel. Not now.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Must you hold up Six of Crows as the bar for everything?<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Do we love Taylor Swift?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509201490ra/24299622.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nice Natalie: It's not all bad. There's good diversity representation. Asher—handsome, sought after Asher—uses a wheelchair. Don't forget the other PoC from a range of different cultures and countries. Hideo, the love interest, is Asian, too.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Thank you for bringing Hideo, I almost forgot. <i>Why did he</i> fall for Emika? The gal I get—he's her idol and made all her dreams come true. Him, ehhh.<br><br>Nice Natalie: What's not to like about her? She speaks her mind and is a brilliant hacker.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Yes. Because there's no way Hideo has come across an independent, sassy woman once in his course as CEO of a multi-billion dollar company.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Do you not have a romantic bone in your body?<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Not in my body, no. But I do have a pretty nice collection in my basement.<br><br>Before you get all moony-eyed, remember we guessed all the twists, including one that was so soap-opera-ish, I still can't believe Lu included it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Zero is Sasuke. That is so embarrassing, I'm getting secondhand heat waves <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Nice Natalie: Just because we know how a story is going to end, it doesn't spoil the journey. We were really happy when we spotted all those Easter eggs from her previous books: a Warcross team named Windwalkers; Asher's big brother is called Daniel Wing; and the merit system in Japan, where you earn points for doing something small like watering a plant, mimics that of Antarctica from Legend's dystopian setting. Warcross is like a distant prequel. Lu confirmed it on her Twitter, too.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Big deal.<br><br>Nice Natalie: It is a big deal. That earns half a star at least.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: Oh no, you don't. We're going to be objective. Two stars and that's because I'm happy Taylor Swift's Reputation is coming out in two weeks.<br><br>Nice Natalie: Two stars are for books we hate!<br><br>Cynical Natalie: No, one star is for books we hate. But since you insist, one star.<br><br>Nice Natalie: No!<br><br>Cynical Natalie: 0.5. Do I hear a bid for 0.5?<br><br>Nice Natalie: At least make it a solid four.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: In your glitter-powdered dreams. Two, take it or leave it.<br><br>Nice Natalie: THREE. And an extra 0.5 because we really do love you, Marie. I'm sorry I can't do more.<br><br>Cynical Natalie: I'm not. Now where's my Taylor t-shirt? I got Tumblr shit to reblog.<br><br>Other Nice Natalie/Cynical Natalie <s>brawls</s> reviews:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/372646324" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940598996" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreams of Gods &amp; Monsters</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/915207283" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Stay</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989706383" rel="nofollow noopener">A Girl Like You</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933780638" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1272063698" rel="nofollow noopener">Me and Earl and the Dying Girl</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281202430" rel="nofollow noopener">Catching Fire</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1255504583" rel="nofollow noopener">All The Rage</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277898365" rel="nofollow noopener">An Ember In The Ashes</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543869637" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter &amp; the Cursed Child</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432310" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hammer of Thor</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1478432316" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ship of the Dead</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758536754" rel="nofollow noopener">Caraval</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1607433529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1607433529" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1607433529?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1607433529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15523619788384809185"><blockquote>
  <i>Imagine wandering through the most realistic virtual Paris ever, or lounging in a full simulation of Hawaii’s beaches. Imagine flying through a fantasy world of dragons and elves. Anything.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Tokyo. Virtual reality. Spies.</b> Do I really need to say anymore?<br/><br/>Oh okay, I guess I'll say some more. Aside from a few kinks that will probably be ironed out by the final publication, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_' title='Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Warcross</a> is a <b>thrilling sea of action</b> and <b>exciting sci-fi possibility</b>. It presents a world that, given our current technology</span>
  <span id="freeText15523619788384809185" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Imagine wandering through the most realistic virtual Paris ever, or lounging in a full simulation of Hawaii’s beaches. Imagine flying through a fantasy world of dragons and elves. Anything.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Tokyo. Virtual reality. Spies.</b> Do I really need to say anymore?<br /><br />Oh okay, I guess I'll say some more. Aside from a few kinks that will probably be ironed out by the final publication, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Warcross</a> is a <b>thrilling sea of action</b> and <b>exciting sci-fi possibility</b>. It presents a world that, given our current technology, doesn't seem that implausible at all, and in this world, Lu introduces a plot full of secrets and lies, friends and enemies, and the promise of even better things to come.<br /><br />Emika Chen is a college dropout, hacker and bounty hunter in New York City. Ever since her beloved father died, she struggles to keep a roof over her head by catching the petty criminals who the police put out rewards for. Then one day she gets desperate and takes a risky opportunity to earn some quick cash - by hacking into the live Warcross opening ceremony on the Neurolink. Unfortunately, or fortunately, she gets caught.<br /><br />Warcross is a virtual reality combat game created by young billionaire, Hideo Tanaka. Almost everyone plays around the world, and the live championships are watched by all. Teams compete in virtual arenas to steal the opposing team's artifact. When Emika hacks into Warcross, she thinks she's in big trouble, so it comes as a huge surprise when Hideo offers her an undercover job as a player (and a spy) in the game.<br /><br />It is a very visual book, full of <b>stunning world descriptions</b> as the players find themselves in new and exciting arenas. But as well as this, Lu knows her audience well, and she infuses everything with bloodthirsty action and competition, somewhere halfway between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a> and a good ol' game of Quidditch. <br /><br />Of course, Emika's digging into the dangerous underbelly of the hacker world will reveal some dark truths and cause her ever more problems. I predicted one thing that would happen, but never foresaw the other big reveal. And my predictions were not really disappointing - they just made me even more eager to know what happens next.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Warcross</a> is also a <b>beautifully diverse book</b>. Emika is Chinese-American, Hideo is Japanese, the captain of Emika's Warcross team is in a wheelchair, and Roshan and Tremaine are gay. The international appeal of the game gives Lu the opportunity to include people of all colours and backgrounds - an opportunity she does not pass up.<br /><br />I feel like the few rough patches will be fixed in the final version, but maybe I'll have to pick up a library copy to find out. There were a couple of things towards the end that felt poorly-explained. Such as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[why the end of the game was a trigger <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hideo's real explanation for why he hired Emika. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But these were not big issues.<br /><br />The ending sets the book up for what looks to be a fantastic sequel. I even think there is room for Lu to explore some <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13615.Death_Note__Vol__1_Boredom__Death_Note___1_" title="Death Note, Vol. 1 Boredom (Death Note, #1) by Tsugumi Ohba" rel="nofollow noopener">Death Note</a>-esque moral ambiguity if she's feeling adventurous, which I really hope she is. I can't wait.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15523619788384809185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3543998664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3543998664" />
    <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader"><img alt="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550626778p2/8114361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3543998664?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader">Jesse (JesseTheReader)</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3543998664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11114062880068693672">I wish I would have read this sooner! I loved how visually stunning the world was and how cinematic the writing was. It was so easy to picture in my head and it was an overall well paced story. I will say that nothing really surprised me while reading it. It was kind of easy to decipher the mystery aspect of the book, but it was still a really enjoyable read. <br/><br/><br/>(I also can't believe I didn't know it took place in Japan! I would've bumped it to the top of my tbr asap had I known!) </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <i>Everything's science fiction until someone makes it science fact.</i>
  </i>
</blockquote>Emika Chen - bounty hunter, hacker, programmer, liar - is <b>about to lose everything. </b><br><br>In typical YA fashion, <b>her parents are nowhere to be found</b> (dead father and abandoned by her mother), she's scarily good at many, many things and she's just<b> desperate enough to risk </b>all she has left.<blockquote>
  <i>It is hard to describe loss to someone who has never experienced it, impossible to explain all the ways it changes you. But for those who have, not a single word is needed.</i>
</blockquote>Emika is about to be kicked out of her apartment and so decides to<b> hack into Warcross </b>- a virtual reality game that uses dreams to make the game as realistic as possible. <blockquote>
  <i>Why would anyone give up the perfect fantasy reality just because they have to give up their freedom? What’s the point of freedom if you’re just living in a miserable reality?</i>
</blockquote>She's already<b> incredibly good at the game</b> (despite her low ranking) and knows that the various "power-ups" have real-world value. <br><br>During the annual Warcross games, she notices a power-up worth enough cash to tempt anyone and so hacks herself into the game.<br><b><br>Only it goes wrong. </b><br><br>Her invisible hack suddenly broadcasts her location to the millions of people watching the games.<br><br>Much to her surprise, instead of being arrested, the game's creator (Hideo) <b>offers her a job</b> - to find an elusive player bent on wreaking havoc on the Warcross games. <br><br>He's absurdly young considering the empire he's created, and Emika may just be feeling a little bit of something for him.<blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe they think I'm a danger to you."<br>He smiles as he reaches me. "And are you?"<br>"I try to restrain myself," I answer, returning his smile.</i>
</blockquote>She quickly signs up, relocates to Tokyo and infiltrates one of the Warcross teams...only to learn that <b>things are far more sinister</b> than she ever imagined... <br><br>But if one thing's for certain,<b> Emika is not a quitter.</b> She will follow this through...to the very end.<blockquote>
  <i>But I've never been good at following instructions. I'm a bounty hunter. And if my bounty's still out there somewhere, I have to finish this.</i>
</blockquote><b>This one was good...just not as<i> stunning</i> as I expected.</b><br><br>So many people recommended this one and while I enjoyed it...<b>it felt just a bit cookie-cutter.</b><br><br><b>Mysterious-unknown girl</b> is super good at a very obscure skill set that just-so-happens to be exactly what <b>rich-and-gorgeous boy wants.</b><br><br>She is immediately attracted, and so is he, but they both cannot help but wonder if the other will betray them.<br><br><b>
  <i>Drama and intrigue </i>
</b>surround them from all sides - no one is to be trusted but trust she must in order to survive.<br><br>Essentially, <b>my eyes hurt from <i>rolling</i> so much. </b><br><br>Again, it's not horrible, it just didn't feel particularly new or engaging. It was just felt like something I've read before (and not in a good way).<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Nancy Wu and wow, she was impressive. Fabulous!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9392877461305460986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2104696450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2104696450" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2104696450?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=competition">competition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104696450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16949412564944182340">Warcross is more than just a game. It’s an industry. It’s a way of life. It’s unlimited access to the future. <br/><br/>And for Emika, Warcross has recently become her saviour… and job. <br/><br/>I have to say, Marie Lu can truly write anything. Dystopian, fantasy or science fiction, it doesn’t matter, Marie Lu can do it all. I’m surprised she hasn’t written a contemporary book yet, though I admit her thing is action and complex worlds, so I’m glad she’s sticking to those departments. <br/><br/>WARCROSS is so unlike her prev</span>
  <span id="freeText16949412564944182340" style="display:none">Warcross is more than just a game. It’s an industry. It’s a way of life. It’s unlimited access to the future. <br /><br />And for Emika, Warcross has recently become her saviour… and job. <br /><br />I have to say, Marie Lu can truly write anything. Dystopian, fantasy or science fiction, it doesn’t matter, Marie Lu can do it all. I’m surprised she hasn’t written a contemporary book yet, though I admit her thing is action and complex worlds, so I’m glad she’s sticking to those departments. <br /><br />WARCROSS is so unlike her previous works, and yet, I recognized her touch. It’s professionally-written, with a serious atmosphere, and a badass heroine you’ll root for. <br /><br />Is it weird that I liked the main villain as much as Emika herself? He’s just the right type you love to hate. Even the love interest didn’t hold a candle to him. <br /><br />Actually, there’s nothing I disliked about this book… except that I didn’t fall for the romance. It wasn’t rushed, but it was expected. Furthermore, a man in power falling for a woman in need of help does not do it for me. <br /><br />Everything else, though, I savoured. I enjoyed reading about the Warcross game so badly I wanted to experience it myself. It does sound astounding. It’s funny because I’m not a gamer and I’ve never been into virtual reality or WoW-ish worlds. <br /><br />But this game fascinated me, especially Emika’s role in it. The way she used the elements of the game to attempt to capture Zero showed intelligence and a curious mind. <br /><br />The other players in Emika’s team should have been more developed. Their voices sounded true, but we know extremely little about them. Emika herself wasn’t so interested in her teammates, so that has to change… and I have a feeling it will.<br /><br />Such shocking final events. I saw some of them coming, but mostly, a truck mercilessly ran me over. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16949412564944182340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056226381?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056226381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5745472904084604974">I have a really important question.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/12/05/warcross-review-i-will-never-like-anything-ever-also-im-back/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>Like, everything I say is really important, and therefore every question I ask is really important, but this is especially so. It is integral to my understanding of the world around me, and also books and also Goodreads.<br/><br/>Is there a single person who gave this book over 3 stars and has read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ready Player One</a>?<br/><br/>Seriously. This book is a C-, young adult, romance-y, boring, poorly-built version of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ready Player One</a>. With better di</span>
  <span id="freeText5745472904084604974" style="display:none">I have a really important question.<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2017/12/05/warcross-review-i-will-never-like-anything-ever-also-im-back/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>Like, everything I say is really important, and therefore every question I ask is really important, but this is especially so. It is integral to my understanding of the world around me, and also books and also Goodreads.<br><br>Is there a single person who gave this book over 3 stars and has read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a>?<br><br>Seriously. This book is a C-, young adult, romance-y, boring, poorly-built version of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a>. With better diversity.<br><br>I was always worried about this book literally just straight up being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a>. Just kidding that is completely a lie. I was always super full-on hoping this book was going to be an absolute imitation of that one, because that book is amazing and I miss it all the time and I would like every book I read to be just like it please and thanks.<br><br>What I should have been worried about, and am now furious over (if furious means “just vaguely disappointed because I have hated so many books I’ve been excited for that an overwhelming numbness has taken over what used to be the anger factory that is my emotions”), is that this book would be a lesser, watered-down, poorly <i>done</i> version of that book.<br><br>I will back up for a moment.<br><br>Warcross takes place in the future. (How quaint.) There’s an augmented reality gaming type deal (wish I could tell you more) called Warcross (surprise! Title!). Everybody is super into it. To play, you wear a pair of glasses that overlay the interface into your actual brain. <br><br>If this sounds at all familiar, you have probably encountered the synopsis of a lil book called Ready Player One at some point or another.<br><br>Specifically, Warcross (book not game) is about this gal named Emika, who is a bounty hunter in New York City. This should be cool, and is instead something we hear about for roughly 5 pages. To compare, we hear exponentially more about Emika’s ramen stash (she tells us how many boxes she has seemingly upwards of one thousand times), her urine-scented hovel of an apartment building, and her rainbow hair. <br><br>WE ARE REMINDED SO CONSTANTLY THAT EMIKA HAS RAINBOW HAIR THAT I THINK THE AUTHOR MUST HAVE CONSCIOUSLY CHOSEN TO INSERT A DESCRIPTION OF IT EVERY TIME SHE WONDERED WHETHER EMIKA SHOULD HAVE A SINGLE PERSONALITY TRAIT. Just, <i>Nah. She doesn’t need both a personality AND cool hair. How rad can one person be?</i><br><br>There’s that comforting burn of anger! You guys. We’re doing it.<br><br>Okay. So on top of being a bounty hunter, rainbow-haired, AND ramen-possessing (what a jack of all trades), Emika is also totally amazing at all things computer-related. She hacks! (We have no idea what goes into hacking beyond the oft-used description, <i>I pulled up a window and typed a few lines of code</i>, but sure!) She is really good at Warcross! (We only get one actual scene of an actual game of Warcross, but yeah, okay!) She can try to steal an expensive power-up from an internationally-broadcast game watched by hundreds of millions of people and instead just broadcast her image to all of them! (I don’t get why this is impressive rather than a somewhat sloppy and definitely ill-advised attempt at theft, but sounds good!)<br><br>Emika is so talented and brilliant and rainbow-haired that she is hired by Hideo, the young, dashing, unbelievably boring creator of Warcross. Now, she’s a bounty hunter who is also a hacker who is also playing in the international tournament of an augmented reality game! Doesn’t that sound interesting?<br><br>Don’t get excited. It is not interesting.<br><br>Unless your idea of interesting is the two most boring people in the mapped universe falling gushily in love with each other, except worse. Because Emika constantly has to sneak in order to squeeze in more of these gazing-into-each-other’s-Warcross-lens-wearing-eyes moments.<br><br>It is stressful to read about. It is also a constant reminder that she is physically exiting what could be an interesting plotline in favor of horrific, cavity-inducing romance over and over. And over. And over. And over again.<br><br>I really do not even understand what Warcross is. It’s called a game a lot, but it seems like it might be a version of reality wherein gaming is an option? I don’t know how often the characters of this book are in-game versus in life. I don’t know what the in-life body looks like while the brain is in-game. I thought that Emika was physically traveling to all these places, but at one point towards the end it’s just like, “The screen faded to black and I was back in my hotel room,” and I was all, WAIT WAS SHE IN HER HOTEL ROOM THE WHOLE TIME?<br><br>I have no answers. Because the world-building in this book is <i>terrible</i>.<br><br>Even if I give the author the benefit of the doubt and say she was trying to seamlessly weave in the world-building (admirable!), there is still no excuse for this. Warcross is so confusing that it hurts my brain. Not because it is a really complicated world, but because it is NEVER EXPLAINED. I don’t get how I could like this setting, because I don’t know what it is.<br><br>Which leads me back to the question that started this review. HAVE YOU GUYS NOT READ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002" rel="nofollow noopener">READY PLAYER ONE</a>? If you had, there is no way you would be so heavy into this game. (IS IT A GAME.) It is millennia behind the description and comprehensibility and interesting-ness of the sometimes-game of that book. (SEE? I KNOW IT’S A SOMETIMES-GAME.)<br><br>So we’ve covered the crap world-building. We’ve covered the awful romance, although I could scream about that for 8 more pages and am merely rescuing you from the fate of hearing me read about it. What else, what else.<br><br>Ah, yes! This book is so boring that it makes watching paint dry seem like a fun way to spend a Saturday afternoon. It makes BBC miniseries focusing on the vie quotidienne of the 19th century seem concerningly wild. It makes Hideo seem like a pre-engagement Prince Harry. Like, back when he used to be naked all the time, and in Las Vegas and stuff.<br><br>This book is non-online clickbait. It pulls you in with the talk of virtual reality, and gaming, and the future, and sci-fi, and bounty hunters, and all that fun stuff, and then it spends the entirety of its 368 pages finding new creative ways to beat all of that with rocks and spears and sharp things until it is so dry your eyes will stream silent tears.<br><br>For example. Even though this book allegedly takes place over the course of a massive, huge-deal, très competitive Warcross tournament that is so blindingly entertaining that hundreds of millions of people tune in for what is cumulatively dozens of hours of watching other people play video games, WE ONLY TRULY SEE ONE ACTUAL TYPICAL GAME.<br><br>This is the best scene in the book, by far, yes, but it is <i>roughly 20 pages of what I thought all 368 would be.</i> This scene doesn’t even come until, like, the halfway point. And from there until the end, it’s all boring, nondescriptive insertions of Emika doing stuff that is not as cool as Warcross, and romance. And more romance. And more romance.<br><br>Also the “big reveals” of this book are either a) revealed in the very beginning (I was actually like, <i>There’s no way, she’ll find out it’s someone else, it’s way too early - but nope</i>) or dropped like huge bombs and then completely left there.<br><br>You guys! This book is so bad.<br><br>That being said, I’ll almost definitely read the next one.<br><br>Bottom line: Just...just do yourself a favor and read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1993608002" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> instead.<br><br><br>------------<br>PRE-REVIEW<br><br>Have I been pranked?<br><br>Did someone give me a different book called Warcross? Have all of you pretended to love this one? Is there an included supplementary text on the world that I missed out on? Does my version somehow contain a mega-expanded first half and a minimized second?<br><br>I have a sneaking suspicion that the answer to all of these questions is no.<br><br>And if so...this book was Not Great.<br><br>Review to come<br><br>------------<br><br>IT'S FINALLY HAPPENING.<br><br>------------<br><br>I want this so badly that I've been daydreaming about illegally downloading it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500701588ra/23374279.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5745472904084604974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText908012286723421808" style="display:none">DNF at 50% - audiobook <br /><br />Pretty much from the beginning, I wasn’t too thrilled about this book. The main character is just so bland. <br /><br />Poor orphan girl who becomes the chosen one for a talent that feels like she got overnight. We're never told how she actually got great at hacking. She basically unfocuses her eyes and things stand out to her... Maybe I'm bitter because I was never able to do that with the Garfield book I had! <br />But *gaps* she has a record!! For doing a nice thing… Does it mean she's not like other girls? <br />Let's be real, giving her rainbow hair won’t hide how bland she is.<br /><br />But the last drop for me was when the romance that started. I get it, he's her idol that makes sense but he has no reason to be into her. When the interactions started being cringy I just decided to DNF the whole thing.<br /><br />Life's too short for cringy YA romance book with a predictable plot. It had potential but... no. <div id="review_2156150190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156150190" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156150190?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156150190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4584299555953138562"><i>Think. You can solve this. This will not be your life. You are not destined to stay here forever. You are not your father.</i><br/><br/>This is easily the most <b>brilliant, exciting, and action packed</b> novel I've read in 2017. If I wasn't a <s>responsible</s> adult, I would have blown through this in a single sitting. I'll admit, I had seen talk of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_' title='Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Warcross</a> filling my feed here for well over six months prior to it's release date, but was a bit skeptical. Reading the blurb gave me a feeling of "been there, done that mor</span>
  <span id="freeText4584299555953138562" style="display:none"><i>Think. You can solve this. This will not be your life. You are not destined to stay here forever. You are not your father.</i><br /><br />This is easily the most <b>brilliant, exciting, and action packed</b> novel I've read in 2017. If I wasn't a <s>responsible</s> adult, I would have blown through this in a single sitting. I'll admit, I had seen talk of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Warcross</a> filling my feed here for well over six months prior to it's release date, but was a bit skeptical. Reading the blurb gave me a feeling of "been there, done that more times than I can count", but I was so intrigued by the consistently high ratings that my curiosity stayed piqued. After attending the Goodreads Summit in October and several friends gushing over it being their favorite book of the year, I knew it was time to pick it up and see what all the fuss is about. I am so delighted that I listened to the experts, because this was truly a favorite read of mine for many reasons. <br /><br /><i>Warcross was pretty simple: two teams battled each other, one trying to take the other team's Artifact (a shiny gem) without losing their own. What made it spectacular were the virtual worlds the battles were set in, each one so realistic that putting on your glasses was like dropping you right into that place. </i><br /><br />What can I say that hasn't already been said? I feel like once you know the basic gist of the story you've got what you need going into it. I actually picked this up without reading the summary again (the last time I did was probably 3 months ago) and I love the open perspective it gave me. I had no preconceived notions, no expectations or spoiler-filled thoughts; I simply dove in and hung on for the ride. And what a ride it was! The descriptions, atmosphere, and setting in this book were so intricate in details that I felt as though I were watching a movie in my head rather than reading words on a page. The colors, artistic backgrounds, and global experiences were truly that; experiences. I found my breath catching multiple times, and most were not during the high octane action scenes. I could truly picture this book being turned into a hollywood blockbuster film; my only concern is that we do not have the technology yet to do the story the justice it so richly deserves.<br /><br /><i>If I could solve these problems, then I could control something. And if I could control something, I could forgive myself for the one problem that I could never have solved, the one person I could never have saved. Everyone has a different way of escaping the dark stillness of their mind. This, I learned, was mine. </i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a> is at the top of her game here; she knows how to write characters who are divinely flawed, ones that stir a sense of camaraderie, hope, and consistency, and then manages to break your heart and piece it back together by the end of the book. The subtle, yet natural inclusion of diversity here is stellar; the characters are completely different but the realistic sense reminded me of how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575289.Leigh_Bardugo" title="Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Leigh Bardugo</a> created her gang of lovable nuggets in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33245734.Six_of_Crows" title="Six of Crows by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows</a> (Squad Goals). We have representation of multiple races, LGBT, and disabilities that make for a well crafted group whom rely on each other for different strengths and weaknesses. I can't express how much this touched my heart, as I feel like it is STILL so difficult to find this type of essential diverseness in current fiction. <br /><br />There's not much else to add, although I had a few jaw-dropping moments near the end. There are a few big twists, one of which I suspected and one that completely blew my mind, but the story in it's entirety is worthy of all five stars regardless of your deduction skills. This is the type of thrilling science fiction/dystopian that is effortlessly enjoyed by all, regardless of age, race, gender, etc. This is a fantastic entry to a new world that I look forward to visiting again; the ending was left beautifully ready for the sequel and I'll be keeping my fingers crossed that it lives up to the hype. <s>And that it has a more appealing cover.</s></span>
  <a data-text-id="4584299555953138562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1703012025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703012025" />

<span id="freeTextContainer17594663583717976890">Oh man. Marie Lu KILLED it. This was phenomenal, and easily one of my favorite books of 2017. <br/><br/>I don't even want to say much about the plot (hah if you know me, I normally like to go into books blind anyway). I'll just say this - Emika is a kick ass heroine struggling to survive in a world where digital reigns.   <span id="freeText17594663583717976890" style="display:none">Oh man. Marie Lu KILLED it. This was phenomenal, and easily one of my favorite books of 2017. <br /><br />I don't even want to say much about the plot (hah if you know me, I normally like to go into books blind anyway). I'll just say this - Emika is a kick ass heroine struggling to survive in a world where digital reigns. But she does something unexpected, which leads to a domino of events that land her in a crazy cool situation with the maker of Warcross. <br /><br />Thats it. That's all you get. <br /><br />Hah okay but seriously... I am not a huge sci fi/futuristic/dystopian (not sure if this is actually dystopian though) fan. I'm a fantasy reader, point blank period. However, I LOVED Ready Player One, mostly because I played World of Warcraft for years when I was in college (heyo to my gamer friends.) And if you've read Ready Player One, you know its the perfect balance between fun references to crazy intense plot line, and it appeals to an audience beyond the themes it references. It was a freaking great story. <br /><br />The same can be said about this.<br /><br />Right now, my husband is actually reading my ARC of this and loving it. Like when we read Ready Player One together, he's constantly nudging me and freaking out because Marie Lu knows her stuff. (Oh my gosh there's a certain reference to WoW that had me actually screaming.)<br /><br />But even if you have no gamer knowledge or you're intimidated by books like this - trust me, don't pre judge it. The story is damn fun and full of feels. Marie Lu has a way of sucking you into her characters, and her writing is so easy to follow. Not to mention, this is one of the coolest worlds I've read about, and Emika is so thoroughly developed in the beginning of the book that you're instantly drawn to her and rooting for her hardcore. <br /><br />You guys, I enjoyed EVERY. SINGLE. PAGE. The whole book is so well written and holy crap, I think I jumped out of my bed a few times. Oh man. I wish I could say more, but there are some FUN plot twists. I guessed a few, but oh Marie Lu got me in the end. But try not to go in with expectations. Just get pulled along with the plot and have fun.<br /><br />AND HOLY CRAP SLDFKJ:SLKFDJ BOOK TWO AHHHH I NEED IT NOWWWW. That set up... ermergershalkdjfal;skdfj.<br /><br /><br />***<br /><br />Initial pre-review:<br /><br />If you like Ready Player one, read this book.<br />If you didn't like Ready Player one, read this book.<br />If you read only fantasy(like me), trust me, take a break from it and read this book.<br />If you liked this book, read Ready Player one (once the trauma wears down.) And then come off the high of RP1 and read this book.<br /><br />Basically read this book.<br /><br />...<br />What the hell am I supposed to do now???<br /><br />AL;KSDJFAL;SKDJF<br /><br />Review to come. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_1569136989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1569136989" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1569136989?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1569136989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14012805538939917432"><b>4.5</b> and all my love.<br/><br/><b>“... but tonight, I can join in with everyone else, put on my glasses, and watch magic happen.”</b><br/><br/>Do you remember Antarctica in <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14290364.Champion__Legend___3_' title='Champion (Legend, #3) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Champion</a>?</i> How that world worked? Since the moment I read that, I've hoped Marie Lu would take that concept and expand it somehow. And then she did. So I mean it literally when I say that <b><i>Warcross</i> made my dreams come true</b>. <br/><br/>•<i>Warcross</i> might not be the best book you'll ever read. It might not be the most profound, or the most complex, or the most clever. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText14012805538939917432" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b> and all my love.<br /><br /><b>“... but tonight, I can join in with everyone else, put on my glasses, and watch magic happen.”</b><br /><br />Do you remember Antarctica in <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14290364.Champion__Legend___3_" title="Champion (Legend, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Champion</a>?</i> How that world worked? Since the moment I read that, I've hoped Marie Lu would take that concept and expand it somehow. And then she did. So I mean it literally when I say that <b><i>Warcross</i> made my dreams come true</b>. <br /><br />•<i>Warcross</i> might not be the best book you'll ever read. It might not be the most profound, or the most complex, or the most clever. But it sure stands a good chance of being the most <b>entertaining, exciting, engaging and thrilling</b>. It made my body release so much adrenaline I don't know how my heart didn't stop. I love the concept and how it was staged, I loved the atmosphere, I loved the camaraderie, the team chemistry, the choice to highlight <b>the sense of community Warcross, just like all sports, creates among people all over the world</b>, people from different places and ethnicities and backgrounds yet brought together by something as simple as a game, as simple as the fun they have watching or playing it. It's beautiful. It's one of the most beautiful things in the world, feeling part of a group of people who share their love for something joyful and healthy like sports and games. I am beyond glad Marie Lu chose to represent it. <br /><br />•But <i>Warcross</i> isn't just a master of entertainment. Its <b>characters</b> are delicious, <b>well-written, not particularly shaded but just enough to be convincing and compelling</b>. I think<b> this is Marie Lu's secret</b>: she keeps things simple (mind you, I didn't say <i>too</i> simple) but she does everything with such good taste, such sense of measure, a touch peculiar to her that is worth, with its neatness and tastefulness, all the tortuosity in the world. This is true intelligence, if you ask me. <br /><br />•In addition, as she did to a higher degree in <i>The Young Elites</i>, Marie Lu doesn't resist <b>crafting her characters with her trademark blend of light and darkness</b>. I loved <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hideo's character and his twisted plan <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I love it all the more it's not as if I don't see his reasons; on the contrary, I can see them all too well. When I least expected it, when I had started to believe it was all about <i>the game</i>, this book raised the stakes and led me even to question myself, to wonder what I would have done in his shoes. It was a <b>plot-twist </b>that surprised me as much as it pleased me. <br /><br />➽ Well, let's see, how can I put this... <b>I need the sequel now</b>. <b>I worship Marie Lu</b>. If the conclusion proves to be better than <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588345.The_Midnight_Star__The_Young_Elites___3_" title="The Midnight Star (The Young Elites, #3) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Star</a>,</i> then this series (duology, I believe?) might even become my favourite of Marie Lu's works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14012805538939917432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
