<span id="freeTextContainer9183085225583511863"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507285802i/24099461._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love Marie Lu, but I had a hard time with this book in the beginning. I felt like I wasn't really going to get into this book. I have to say it took almost until the end to really enjoy it. I'm not sure if it was my mood, that I wasn't really ready for a gaming book or what. Either way, I did enjoy it after I kept going. <br/><br/>What I want to know now, is that ending? What is going to happen in the next book? I mean who do you trust now? <br/><br/>It was pretty obvious to me right up front who the hacker in Wa</span>
  <span id="freeText9183085225583511863" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507285802i/24099461._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Marie Lu, but I had a hard time with this book in the beginning. I felt like I wasn't really going to get into this book. I have to say it took almost until the end to really enjoy it. I'm not sure if it was my mood, that I wasn't really ready for a gaming book or what. Either way, I did enjoy it after I kept going. <br><br>What I want to know now, is that ending? What is going to happen in the next book? I mean who do you trust now? <br><br>It was pretty obvious to me right up front who the hacker in Warcross was that wanted to take out the creator, Hideo Tanka. <br><br>Emika Chen is a bounty hunter and a hacker. She hacked into the Warcross game and everyone saw her. Ooops. You put on these like sunglasses and get into the game and she jumped right into a tournament and stopped the game. Well, things obviously change after that because Hideo has sent for her. <br><br>Hideo pays off Emika's debts and hires her to find out who is hacking into this game. There is a killer among us. He puts her in the game as a player and it's all go from there. <br><br>So the supposed assassin came as no surprise but the things he said did. . . . Now I have to wait until the next freaking book to find out if it's all real or just another game . . . . <br><br>. . . .<br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/10/warcross-by-marie-lu.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2064084874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2064084874" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2064084874?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241321447" href="/book/show/37771077-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=young-adult-series">young-adult-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2064084874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9861478517114286007"><i>”Everything’s science fiction until someone makes it science fact,” Hideo says.</i><br/><br/>Well, okay, after taking a closer look at my friend’s reviews I guess it’s time for another unpopular opinion from me. I really wanted to love this and I suppose in some ways I even did, if I’m entirely honest I wasn’t as blown away by the book as everyone else seems to be though. >_<<br/><br/>After reading <b>“The Young Elites”</b> Marie Lu became one of my favourite authors and I really love and appreciate that series but <b>“Warcross”</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9861478517114286007" style="display:none"><i>”Everything’s science fiction until someone makes it science fact,” Hideo says.</i><br /><br />Well, okay, after taking a closer look at my friend’s reviews I guess it’s time for another unpopular opinion from me. I really wanted to love this and I suppose in some ways I even did, if I’m entirely honest I wasn’t as blown away by the book as everyone else seems to be though. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />After reading <b>“The Young Elites”</b> Marie Lu became one of my favourite authors and I really love and appreciate that series but <b>“Warcross”</b> just didn’t do it for me. Maybe it was because I read “Ready Player One” before I picked up her book or maybe I’ve become just too good at anticipating plot twists? *lol* Either way I wasn’t really surprised by the things that happened and even though it was a lot of fun to guess and wonder about what would happen next, there was something missing while I read the book.<br /><br /><i>”But sometimes, you find yourself standing in exactly the right position, wielding exactly the right weapon to hit back. So I hit. I hit fast and hard and furious. I hit with nothing but the language whispered between circuits and wire, the language that can bring people to their knees.<br />And in spite of everything, I’d do it all over again.”</i><br /><br />I liked the characters but for some reason I didn’t connect to them. I loved that Lu had so much diversity in this book but felt unhappy about the fact that it wasn’t explored, it was rather some sort of side note in the main plot and didn’t get any room. I enjoyed the idea of pop culture references but when I read about them they were always rendered anonymous. Like for instance there would be the mention of a lost city under water as one of the worlds they fight in. Why not call it Atlantis? Why not call the beverages they drink by name? Wouldn’t it have been easier to say they drink idk Cherry Coke instead of a “soft drink with ….”? <br /><br /><i>”Every other team is going to underestimate you. They’ll say I’ve lost my touch, that I picked you just for the news coverage it’ll get the Riders. But we know better than that, don’t we? I don’t waste my time on players with no potential. You’re a weapon in disguise – and I intend to keep it that way until our first game.”</i><br /><br />But then again, maybe this was the reason why so many people liked it more than “Ready Player One”!? I mean the pop culture references in RPO are aplenty and always called by name and I know for fact that there are a lot of people who didn’t like this. *lol* Still, I could smell some of the plot twist from miles away and therefore wasn’t as shocked as I should have been when they were eventually revealed. <br /><br /><i>”You’re more dangerous than I thought,” Hideo muses, admiring my handiwork.<br />I offer him a smile. “I promise I’ll be nice to you.”<br />This time, I manage to coax a laugh from him. “Should I be even more concerned?” he says to me.</i><br /><br />As for the characters: I liked Emika, but I loved Asher and Roshan. Unfortunately they didn’t get all too much page time and the book mainly focused on the hunt for Zero and - let’s be blunt here - on the romance between Emika and Hideo. Which was okay, but didn’t really wow me. I guess I’ve just seen this trope way too often. Clever, righteous and poor girl falls in love with a young, rich and reserved billionaire and reveals the different “shades” of his personality. Rings a bell, mhmm? *lol* ;-P<br /><br /><i>”It is hard to describe loss to someone who has never experienced it, impossible to explain all the ways it changes you. But for those who have, not a single word is needed.”</i><br /><br />But Hideo is the way he is for a reason and everything is revealed throughout the book. Well, not everything but enough to get a grasp on his personality and to see how he became the person he is now. Who apparently is a guy that has no sexual desires whatsoever. *LOL* Seriously, Craig and I had a good laugh about the fact that there is so much sexual tension between Emi and Hideo and that it always ends up with nothing because they both seem to have a knack of bringing up serious topics in the most inappropriate times. XD <br /><br />And this, my friends was another thing I just couldn’t ignore. Yes, this is a YA book and yes there is bound to be some romance, but come on Marie Lu!!! This was so unrealistic! If you don’t want them to “have a fun time” on page (I’m being conscious of my young readers here. ;-P) then just go for a fade out and pick up the storyline after, or don’t even let them get all too close. *lol* The bathtub scene? I know no teen that would have stopped when things got THAT steamy!!! (Then again maybe I don’t know enough teens. *lol*) <br /><br />Anyway, we’re not talking about appropriate behaviour and mindfulness here, were talking about teenage hormones that get the better of you, no matter how innocent and sweet you are! *LOL* Because in every teens life there comes a moment like that and it always makes the difference between before and after. ;-) Hormones override logic… well at least most of the time. XD I’m not saying they would have gone all the way, but my reasonable brain tells me that there are a lot of other ways to get to know another person and they don’t have to end blacked out. Or like in the book’s case, end completely abruptly because the MCs suddenly have an important thought that needs to be discussed immediately. XD<br /><br />Anyway, let’s get back to the storyline and the ending. As I already mentioned I expected many of the things that happened and there were only two things that actually surprised me. <br /><br />1.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I never would have expected Tremaine to be one of the other hunters that were hired to find Zero, but I still figured that Zero was Hideo’s brother. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />2.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew Hideo’s Neuro Link was a bad thing and that Zero tried to stop it. What I didn’t expect was the extent of it or the fact that it would be as drastic as it turned out to be in the end. <br /><br /><i>”I’m tired of the horror in the world. So I will force it to end.”</i> <br /><br />I mean woah Hideo!!! That’s playing god! Who decides what is bad and what is not? Will the Neuro Link prevent me from mouthing off to my mother when I’m angry or will it only stop me when I try to rob a bank? Can an algorithm like that gauge human behaviour? And if every notion of misbehaviour is already smashed before it even gets a chance to form, how will this change the people in the world? There’s no free will anymore if you can’t even rap someone’s knuckles if they have the audacity to grab your behind. But then again maybe that person who wanted to grope you can’t even do it anymore because the Neuro Link sees it as a bad thing? Where will it end? It really boggles the mind… <br /><br /><i>”He had confided in me, thinking that perhaps I would be the one person who would side with him. Why wouldn’t I, he must have thought – I understood his loss, and he had understood mine. We’d understood each other … or so we thought.”</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/99779228-craig" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Babygreys</a>! and we had a lot of fun guessing and trying to figure out what would happen next. If I would have read the book on my own I probably wouldn’t have had as much fun though. I think my main problem was that I would have liked for things to be more fleshed out. No matter if it was the characters, the references or the world building. I just wanted to get a real grip on this story and this unfortunately didn’t happen. =S<br /><br />So, this ultimately leaves me with 3,5 stars and the genuine hope that Marie Lu will knock my socks off with book two! ;-)<br />______________________<br /><br />And here I go for another buddy read with the ever awesome <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/99779228-craig" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Babygrey</a>! ;-P<br /><br />It’s time I start reading the library books from my <a href="https://thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2019/08/03/library-hopping-a-huge-book-haul/" rel="nofollow noopener">huge book haul</a> last week and since my heart stopped beating when I found <b>“Warcross”</b> in one of the shelves I decided to read it first! XD<br /><br />I really liked <b>“Ready Player One”</b> and everyone keeps telling me that <b>“Warcross”</b> is even better so my expectations are really high. It’s Marie Lu though! So what could possibly go wrong, right? *lol*<br /><br />Let’s find out and talk about it later. ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9861478517114286007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6274700918326881342">This was a 3-star book for me up until the last 15 pages and just wow.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I'm usually great at predicting endings of books but even I didn't see that coming.   <span id="freeText6274700918326881342" style="display:none">This was a 3-star book for me up until the last 15 pages and just wow.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm usually great at predicting endings of books but even I didn't see that coming. </b><br /><br />Also the main character is named <s>Emika</s> Emi and I wanna know who let her have that name? It's mine. She can't have it. <br /><br />Anyways, Me, Emi, <s>and not the Emi in the book</s> have actually finished a book. I actually remembered how to read!!! I'm just as surprised as you are. <br /><br />I had my problems with it, obviously. I wanted to give it 3 stars for most of my read. But that might have to do with the fact for the two months I've been in this horrendous slump, I've spent more time then I probably should admit watching a group of dudes who suck at video games play video games. I'm not used to finding enjoyment if people playing video games well. If that makes sense? <br /><br />Also Ready Player One exists and my brain really latched onto that mentality. <br /><br />I might write a review. I might not. Who knows?   <span id="freeText7944550840991373975" style="display:none">i wish i could just <i>copy + paste</i> the emotions i'm feeling right now so i could accurately convey my love for this book<br><br><blockquote>
  <blockquote>✘ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://playwarcross.com/">http://playwarcross.com/</a>
</blockquote>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517185411i/24956774._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>honestly it's been a while since a book has made me feel so ♥‿♥ and i don't know if i'm ready to talk about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> yet..... but right now i'm not even capable of doing anything but stare at my wall and think about this book anyways so i might as well be semi-productive and write my review while doing that<br><br>if you don't care about my unnecessarily long in-depth analysis of every single thing i felt while reading this work of art, here are <b>
  <u>some things that might convince you to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a>:</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>◈ <b>ready player one</b> but set in tokyo [!!!!!!!] and also more diverse<br>◈ the main character has 1) rainbow hair 2) a criminal record and 3) an intense love for harry potter<br>◈ have i mentioned that she's a skateboarding bounty hunter and hacker <br>◈ your favorite: a <b>squad</b> that would die for each other and also <i>*cries*</i> <b>team dynamics</b><br>◈ there's a dragon at one point<br>◈ also gigantic fighting roboters???<br>◈ shall i go on</blockquote><br>basically it's everything that my nerd heart ever desired and more<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517187018i/24956860._SY540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <a href="http://gianbautista.tumblr.com/post/165434944532" rel="nofollow noopener">©</a>
  <blockquote>
    <b>Every locked door has a key.<br><i>Every problem has a solution.</i></b>
  </blockquote>
</blockquote><br>i wish i could've recorded a Memory of me reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29385546.Warcross__Warcross___1_" title="Warcross (Warcross, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">warcross</a> so i could cherish it forever but it would solely consist of me lying on the floor constantly sobbing and clutching this book to my chest dramatically<br><br><b>
  <u>CHARACTERS</u>
</b><br>shoutout to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">marie lu</a> for creating such amazing characters, i found myself falling in love with <u>everyone and everyTHING*</u> in this book <i>(*wikki my baby robot can i adopt you)</i><br><br>back when i read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">legend</a> i remember not caring about the characters and suddenly i deeply care for EVERY SINGLE PERSON like what why how did this happen i don't want to get emotionally attached to all of them??? pls stop<br>can i just have even more team dynamics in the sequel i love those<br><br>honestly in the mere 350 pages i managed to get attached to all of them [especially asher........ ASHER 💕💘💖💗💓💞 ALSO ROSHAN!!!! thank you] and i could talk about them forever, but i'm going to restrain myself because i don't have any fangirl fuel left at the moment, i'm exhausted from loving this book to bits and pieces<br><br><b>
  <u>WORLD-BUILDING</u>
</b><br>first of all, ??????????, second of all, ¿¿¿¿¿¿¿¿¿¿<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Some people say that Warcross is just a stupid game. Others say it's a revolution. But for me and millions of others, it's the only foolproof way to forget our troubles."</i>
</blockquote><br>i just love everything about this world. <u>plus points</u>: the <b>dark world</b> is basically a fucked-up version of ketterdam, like when can i visit? can i have more? can book 2 pls take place in the dark world for 97% of the time? pls more gamblers, thieves and criminals? PIRATES, maybe? thank you?<br><br><b>
  <u>VERDICT:</u>
</b><br>a+++, 10/10, beautiful, amazing, action-packed, un-put-downable, easy to read, 5/5 stars, would 1000% recommend, PLEASE READ THIS BOOK!!!! thank you.<br><br>now i'm silmultaneously hella excited for warcross #2 and also scared shitless that anything will happen to my favs in the next book, like pls, be kind @ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">marie lu</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517241243i/24960758._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a href="https://emika-chenn.tumblr.com/post/167412524975/the-scariest" rel="nofollow noopener">©</a><br><br>(4.5 stars!)<br><br><blockquote>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421337572?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421337572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer575087750644111135">this was everything i wish ‘ready player one’ could have been. it wasnt convoluted with high-tech coding jargon or bogged down with gaming references - this was a fun story about a girl who unexpectedly finds herself entered in a global gaming competition. and i really enjoyed this, even though i couldnt care less about gaming. marie lu has an effortless style of writing that makes it so easy to inhale her stories and this was no exception. some components were a bit predictable, but overall thi</span>
  <span id="freeText575087750644111135" style="display:none">this was everything i wish ‘ready player one’ could have been. it wasnt convoluted with high-tech coding jargon or bogged down with gaming references - this was a fun story about a girl who unexpectedly finds herself entered in a global gaming competition. and i really enjoyed this, even though i couldnt care less about gaming. marie lu has an effortless style of writing that makes it so easy to inhale her stories and this was no exception. some components were a bit predictable, but overall this was a fun and enjoyable read! very much looking forward to 'wildcard' later this year!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>4 stars</i>
</b></span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953253116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2551175869671466508"><b>"Do you remember one year when that player - Leeroy something - actually got drafted into the Stormchasers, even though he always just charged in and messed up his entire team's play? My God, he was terrible."</b><br/><br/>You read that right, my loves: Marie Lu references freaking Leeroy Jenkins in her writing. I mean, how could I give this book anything less than all the stars?<br/><br/>When I first finished this book, I was leaning towards 4.5 stars and couldn't decide if I should round up or down, but once I let th</span>
  <span id="freeText2551175869671466508" style="display:none"><b>"Do you remember one year when that player - Leeroy something - actually got drafted into the Stormchasers, even though he always just charged in and messed up his entire team's play? My God, he was terrible."</b><br /><br />You read that right, my loves: Marie Lu references freaking Leeroy Jenkins in her writing. I mean, how could I give this book anything less than all the stars?<br /><br />When I first finished this book, I was leaning towards 4.5 stars and couldn't decide if I should round up or down, but once I let the dust settle a little, I realized this book was honestly 99.3% flawlessness.<br /><br /><b>PLOT ➳➳</b><br />Emika Chen is a hacker and a bounty hunter, struggling to make ends meet by searching out criminals who manipulate the legalities of the worldwide phenomenon, <b>Warcross</b>: an augmented reality game that something like 90% of the world logs into at least weekly. While Emika is incredibly good at what she does, times are hard, and she's about to be homeless when a misplaced hacking move launches her <i>into</i> a very important Warcross game with the entire world watching, and suddenly, she's being swept up into working for the creator of the game himself to hunt down the biggest Warcross criminal yet.<br /><br /><b>SETTING ➳➳</b><br />I loved the world that Marie Lu built in this book, because it's just basically a tweaked version of our own Earth, with a few more technological advancements. The game feels like something that could be an actual possibility over the next few decades, so the suspension of disbelief is <i>really</i> easy to come by when you're reading <i>Warcross</i>. The game itself is magical and incredible, connecting users worldwide in a way that can make them feel as though they're literally in the same room. They can play games, go shopping, or just meander through their daily lives with a little more "fun" than they had before.<br /><br /><b>CHARACTERS ➳➳</b><br />Emika is a <i>really</i> fun narrator. First of all, she's a badass hacker without any of the stereotypical "geek girl" cliches that I've grown to expect from most books involving internet culture. She's not a tomboy, she's confident without being arrogant, she has a social life (and the mentions to her dating life are super sex-positive, which I love, because can we just <i>get over</i> the whole slut-shaming-in-YA idea?); Emika is her own person and she's carving out her place in the world. Even when she develops feelings for the love interest in the story, she never becomes some gooey, lovesick mess - she keeps a good head on her shoulders.<br /><br />There are a slew of side characters in this book, and while most of them don't become tremendously fleshed out, most of them are pretty likable. Hideo is the only character besides Emika who we really learn very much about, but he's an incredibly enjoyable aspect of the story, despite feeling a little blurry and "grey" for most of the book (I constantly found myself second-guessing his motives).<br /><br /><b>GAME MECHANICS ➳➳</b><br />As someone who has been gaming my entire life, including MMO playing, I loved the explanations of how the game worked, the ins and outs of the teams and their missions, the challenges they faced... It was so much fun and felt <i>so</i> authentic! I loved that, during every challenge Emika and her team faced, it was so obvious that Marie is writing from experience.<br /><br /><b>THE TWIST (no spoilers!) ➳➳</b><br />As you know from the plot synopsis, Emika is hired by Hideo to hunt down the mysterious hacker who has been evading Warcross's security measures for some time now. Obviously, being mysterious means the big reveal is a pretty big aspect to the book, so I won't spoil anything, but what I <i>will</i> say is that I had a LOT of feelings about the end of this book, and it is a huge cliffhanger ending, and now I feel like I'm going to basically fret myself half to death while waiting on the release of book #2.<br /><br /><b>FINAL VERDICT ➳➳</b><br />This book is pure amazingness, and I recommend it to any YA reader, but <i>especially</i> a YA reader with a love for video games, because this will be right up your alley and I can almost guarantee that you will enjoy it at least a little bit (but probably a lot).<br /><br /><i>Thank you SO much to Edelweiss and the people at G.P. Putnam's Sons Books for Young Readers for approving me for this ARC! All opinions expressed here are entirely my own.</i><br /><br />You can find this review (and more) on my blog <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/07/23/warcross/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2551175869671466508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1791424767" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791424767" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791424767?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399547966" href="/book/show/29385546-warcross">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791424767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16662500955885677048"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Maybe I was wrong, and maybe someday I'll look back and regret lashing out like that. I'm still not entirely sure why I threw myself into the fire over this specific incident. But sometimes, people kick you to the ground at recess because they think the shape of your eyes is funny. They lunge at you because they see a vulnerable body. Or a different skin color. Or a difficult name. Or a girl. They think that you won't hit back—that you'll just lower your eyes and hide. And sometimes, to </b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16662500955885677048" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Maybe I was wrong, and maybe someday I'll look back and regret lashing out like that. I'm still not entirely sure why I threw myself into the fire over this specific incident. But sometimes, people kick you to the ground at recess because they think the shape of your eyes is funny. They lunge at you because they see a vulnerable body. Or a different skin color. Or a difficult name. Or a girl. They think that you won't hit back—that you'll just lower your eyes and hide. And sometimes, to protect yourself, to make it go away, you do. But sometimes, you find yourself standing in exactly the right position, wielding exactly the right weapon to hit back. So I hit. I hit fast and hard and furious. I hit with nothing but the language whispered between circuits and wire, the language that can bring people to their knees. And in spite of everything, I'll do it all over again.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Marie Lu has done it again!</b> I haven't loved all of her books, but yes, I have enjoyed almost all, except for <i>The Midnight Star.</i> Warcross was no different. I wouldn't call Marie one of my favorite authors, but I will surely read anything she writes and I must say, <b>she's really evil when it comes to endings.</b> Her endings in the books are the kind that leaves you shocked and wanting more, craving for more. When I finished <i>The Rose Society</i>, I was quite impatient waiting for <i>The Midnight Star.</i> The same happened with <i>Legend</i> and <i>Prodigy</i> even though the whole trilogy was released. I just didn't have the whole set. Warcross is not my favorite book of hers, but it is definitely on the top 3.<br /><br /><i>Warcross</i> was a book that kept popping up in my feed. I was so excited when this was announced and I was not able to control my excitement over it. After The Midnight Star, I needed some new Lu. I can't blame my friends for loving this. It's a book with  It also has the main character of a <i>female skater with tattoo's who also has rainbow hair, a criminal record, is a bounty hunter.</i> She also loves Harry Potter and seems like the type of person that would be great to chill with around a city because she wouldn't give a fuck about what people think about her and would be cruising with you with her skateboard (if you can also skate that is). Warcross is not just about these two people, but it sure revolves around them. I've seen many reviews saying Warcross is basically <i>Ready Player One</i> and I can't say that's true or false because I, sadly, have not read that book. With that being said, <b>Warcross revolves around Emika Chen who is a female bounty hunter that catches Warcross players who takes down players betting on the game illegally.</b> She currently lives in an apartment that's she's in debt in which leads to the reason she catches these players—to make money. The game of Warcross is a game everyone actually lives in. It's a game created by Hideo Tanaka, the creator of a game set to be seen as a virtual reality that almost everybody is playing. As the Championships are coming along for this game, Emika has to make some cash quickly in order to stay in her apartment. Her father is dead and her mother left her, so she has to be living on her own and has to find ways to take of herself. With that being said, being the hacker she is, she hacks into the opening of the Warcross game, having everyone see her, including the creator, Hideo. She thought she was in without being seen, but that was not the case. Convinced she will be arrested considering the criminal record she already holds, she's ready to face the penalty she knows will come. But instead of a penalty, she gets a call from Hideo. <br /><br />He has a request for her, and it's a big one. <b>He wants her to be a spy for him.</b> With her hacking skills, Emika would be able to find out who is this hidden figure trying to stop Hideo; the hidden figure giving Hideo the suspicion of a security problem. Emika accepts the offer and heads to Tokyo from New York City. From then, Emika begins to get close to Hideo and learn about him, about his past, and about who he really is. And she might just end up regretting the offer she just took from him that leads to the Warcross empire going downhill.<br /><br /><b>I'd first like to say that Emika Chen is the girl every other girl would want. I mean, she's so sick.</b> I'm not saying she's badass, but she is not the typical YA fictional character. Holding a criminal record and catching illegal Warcross players to make cash while skateboarding is what I call sick and chill. To start off, <b>I loved this.</b> The 4 stars does not mean I didn't love this; I do admit it's 4 stars only because it started off slow and boring for me that it almost got to the point where I was gonna give up. Luckily, I didn't and I'm glad I didn't. Warcross is the virtual reality game I wish we had. I mean, we'd be dying in the game but not in real life and battling against other people around the world that are either a higher or lower game than you honestly sounds so fun. We're really over here getting the same video games that people aren't getting tired of. To be honest, America needs to step up their game in many things. I mean, I don't know if you guys listen and watch kpop but the way those music videos are produced is honestly <b>insane.</b> Compared to America, they have everything down. Many American music videos are featuring the same thing without any message. In kpop, every music video has a message and is connected to the previous video and even videos, all tied to one theory. It's insane! Or, well, I think so. I don't know man but America is really behind on a lot of things we need and so heads up on things we do need. If you keep up with politics and news you would know what I mean. <br /><br />Warcross is still the game we all want to have. The way Marie Lu explained the world-building of the whole place of Tokyo and the way Warcross works is what added to the <b>fun of this book.</b> I wasn't interested in the beginning because everything was just about explaining Warcross and was really, just about Warcross, and I really just wanted to get to the point where Emika hacks into the game and is offered this grand prize by Hideo. Speaking of Hideo, <b>I love him.</b> I do, but I also hate him. What he wanted, what he needed, I just didn't agree with it. That ending was also not what I wanted. I thought he would be different because of how he was with Emika, but of course there had to be one plot twist in the middle and two in the end that just...brought everything down. I mean, the book was still amazing, but what went downhill was just the path Marie chose to go in because of how sad it can make the lovers of this book. Book #2 better fix this problem and if it doesn't, it will definitely not be an enjoyable read for me.<br /><br /><b>Hideo Tanaka</b> A teenager born in Tokyo and raised in London and has a British accent. Rolls up his sleeves to his elbows. <i>That was enough for me.</i> I mean, there are specific people who look good in something specific. Another thing, <b>he cooks for his parents and speaks Japanese to them.</b> I'm a fan of diversity. I haven't read many books about diversity or books featuring it, but when I see there are characters from a different country or are a different color of skin other than white and have blonde hair and blue or green or hazel eyes, <b>I will make sure I read it.</b> He's Japanese but was raised in London and that is such a beautiful combination. Moving on, he speaks Japanese (hurray for following his tradition and culture and not abandoning his parent's language because he was raised in a country in Europe and not Asia) and is very respectful towards them, especially his mother.<br /><br />When I first read a book by Marie, believe it or not, <b>I did not know she was Chinese.</b> I'm not the person that will look at an author or anyone else, really, and just say "Oh they're Asian because they have monolids and look Asian." No, I will actually do my research or find out where they're from or what country they represent. A person can <i>look Asian</i> and actually be Latinx. I have a friend who was born here in the US but her mom was born in Mexico while her dad was born in El Salvador but her and her sister, without sounding offensive and racist, look Asian, but they're not. One thing I do hate about that is that she actually goes along with it. I mean, someone will say "I love your Asian looking eyes" and she'll say "thanks, I love my Asian eyes too" but she's not Asian and does not have the stereotypical monolids. She has double eyelids, I've seen them, and it just bugs me how she keeps the "non-existent Asian culture" when she is clearly Hispanic. <b>Marie Lu was born in Wuxi, China and I did not know.</b> What I loved the most about this diversity is that, really, it's an own-voices book. Not necessarily set in China because it's actually set in New York and then Tokyo, Japan, but it's Asian, and also, Emika is Chinese-American (or I saw) and I think the representation of Asia in this was an important key of everything. <br /><br /><b>Let's discuss diversity.</b> Diversity is what really makes a book special; what makes it unique; what makes it beautiful. The world-building of Warcross and Tokyo was beautiful as how Marie Lu wrote it and I wish I could see it in real life. I have never traveled to Asia (and I'm talking about all of Asia in general, not just the typical and well-known countries of China, Japan, SK and NK, Thailand, etc.) I do want to though and I hope to soon. I have a friend who lives in Singapore and I honestly want to go there to meet her. Anyways, I love how, first, Emika is Chinese-American. Marie was born in China but, I'm guessing, identifies as American too since, according to Wiki, her nationality is American? I thought the nationality couldn't be changed... <br /><br />Anyways, the other thing I love about this is the fan art of it. It is a common and popular thing for Asians to wear face masks (Marie Lu said it herself on an Instagram post when she posted a fanart piece) and the fan art includes Emika wearing a face mask which is a big representation of where she is or where her family is, which is China in this case. Moving on, Hideo is Japanese and speaks Japanese well with his family which is something else I loved. I love it when families keep their tradition—including language, celebrations, and foods—and don't give them up for the ones in the country they reside in. Another thing is that in Tokyo, during the Warcross Championships Ceremony, not everyone was Asian. There was a mix—a German, a Chinese, an American, and also brown-skinned players—and it was all really great reading about it. There's also a disabled character who is a top player of the game and that was another bonus. There was also no racism in this and it was something else I loved. Many people in the real world today are struggling with this as people judge them and mislabel them for their <i>stereotypes</i> because of where they are from, but in this book, Emika had friends who were a mix and none of them were rude against the skin color or size of eyes or country of origin—they were all called a family even when they got on each other's nerves and they were in one of those friendships you wish you had. Speaking of language, Lu included real Japanese words in this and I was so happy to see they weren't just fake and made up Japanese words.<br /><br />I'm not a reader that analyzes everything of a book from the setting, world-building, writing, character development, etc, but I do have to mention the character development in this. <b>Emika had zero character development.</b> I mean, she was already a very knowledgeable hacker that knew the strategies for it and everything, but she also became aware of the trouble in the end. It's like she started noticing what was actually happening in the end. While she didn't have any character development, <b>Hideo had the negative, non-needed development.</b> I mean, he was so precious in the beginning. If you're the kind of romance lover like me that can really just SHIP the main OTP in the story and go along with anything, you will find it cute and adorable what Hideo does for Emika. I mean, the story has some romance in it and it's the perfect amount. It's a sci-fi novel to start off with, so romance is not the expectation of it, but I swear the amount in it was just enough and I was actually looking forward for more. Hideo was so sweet and caring with Emika and was really his own self around her. With her, he wasn't the "well known Warcross creator rich boy that just cared about his game". With Emika, he showed his true colors to her and told her personal stuff which I just found to be cute because in books, when it comes to "bad boys" being all "soft and cute" with their partner, I get all the feelings of just hearing and saying <b>"otp!"</b> everywhere because of how different the character can be. <br /><br /><b>Warcross was fast-paced and action-packed.</b> From beginning to end, it was both, but sadly I was not feeling it in the beginning. I was not doubting my love for Marie but I was thinking I was going to have to put this on hold for a while until I read something else, similar, to get a better feeling about it. Deciding to continue it was not something I regret. I loved how fast-paced this was because it was a book that kept me reading even if I did not enjoy the first 100 pages or so. The action in this (in the game of course) was enough to keep me reading and saying "oh my gosh that just happened". This does include the plot twist that really, took a major turn. <b>There's a character in the book that twists the story around a little and makes it more interesting and more fun to read.</b> His name is Zero and he's the one Hideo has hired Emika for to find out about. This is not a spoiler, neither is the name. It is really mentioned in the first few pages when Emika arrives in Tokyo accepting Hideo's offer. There's just something that happens that might either disappoint you or leave you hanging with your mouth open when you read and find out who this Zero dude is and why is he making the Warcross system so difficult for Hideo. <br /><br />Marie Lu really killed me with this one. I loved Hideo, and I really still do, <b>but Marie is one of those authors that makes you love a character only to hate him (or even her) but still manages to make you love them because you feel bad or you just really...sincerely...love them.</b> I really can't wait for what Marie has in plan for the next book and I can't wait for what Marie has next. I mean, she recently wrote Batman so I lied saying I've read all her books. I still have to read Batman and Champion and then I'll be good. I'm really looking forward for this duology though. It may or may not turn into a trilogy, I don't know, but if she ends the second book with a cliffhanger and decides to end the <i>duology</i> there, I'm really stopping there. There won't be any going back until I find out where this <i>cliffhanger</i> takes me. <br /><br />Honestly, if you were a fan of her Young Elites series, I recommend this. Emika is not as badass as Adelina. Emika is sick and fierce, but I would not say she's badass. Adelina is someone who is trying to survive the heartbreaking and sad moments of her past. I will say both female characters have a past that can't get through and can't forget, <b>but Adelina is more of a character that starts from a weak heart to a strong, bolded, and fierce heart.</b> She does her best to survive on her own and she fights for herself and actually has major character development. She becomes very strong and bold, honest, and won't take no for an answer. Emika, on the other hand, is different. She's more of a character that still needs development and needs to find out what exactly she wants to do and how to do it. Hopefully, she has character development in the next book because even though I said I'm not a reader who analyzes <i>everything</i> in a book including characters and their development, I do notice it. It is not something that will just throw the book for me, but it will be something that leaves me wondering why and how the development didn't happen and just has me questioning the author. Marie, in this case, is an author I trust—I trust she will have Emika change in a good way like she has for all her female characters including Adelina and June.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16662500955885677048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15554142865794444371" style="display:none">Wow! Huge surprise here! I didn't like this book! Bet nobody saw that coming! <br /><br />The shittiest plot twist of 2018 is this: that this book was not my cup of stewed lukewarm tea. The biggest gripe I have is that this actually genuinely interested me for about 80 pages, before it devolved into Fifty Shades Of Dull Turgid Heteros and boring fight scene after boring fight scene after <i>boring fight scene.</i> I can't even be bothered to write a long involved GIF-filled snarky review for some butthurt stans to curl their lips at. <i>She's such a bitch!</i> they'll say, as I lie in bed in my cosy flat with crumbs in my hair and Sudocrem on my fucked up pizza face. Honestly, what would be the point? I didn't buy this book, so I can't even lament the money it cost me. I borrowed it, so it's up to the person who spent her hard earned money to wax about the <i>seven! quid! she! wasted!</i><br /><br />What I will say is that Marie Lu and I have got to part ways. It was never going to work between us, not after The Young Elites. It was never meant to be. I wish her all the happiness in the world, and it's clear that she is an artist with talent. I'm glad she's done so well. I just hated this book. That's all there is to say, really. Slàinte mhath!</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2242082523">
  <td colspan="2">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vFh5EPWUFUBBzIsjfvK2t/3EvQPv6MwLCdwbMEMnwMBQS/IinGWsu638YTWjX6zeOEsRl2Wucnqp8SAUZru0Aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I0Ah3+Ms6qdAqTJFAVnsUVYfB19CdU/crmOem4xF3dHPU6rtit1TXKyZ2FPc9PY4k5Cry8gz8a0OTqW/qdmpEg==')})
  }
//]]>
